[Falco]: Streets, sidewalks, and other public places, article three, sidewalks, section 74-114, entitled Removal of Snow and Ice.

[Falco]: said section presently states section 74-114, removal of snow and ice.

[Falco]: A, whenever the sidewalk or any part of the sidewalk adjoining any building or a lot of land of any street is encumbered with ice and snow, it shall be the duty of the tenant or occupant and in case there should be no tenant or occupant of the whole of such building a lot of land, it shall be the duty of the owner

[Falco]: with a person having care of the sidewalk or to cause such sidewalk to have been made safe, convenient for public use or travel by removing the ice or snow or by covering the area with sand or some other suitable substance.

[Falco]: In case such tenant, occupant, owner, or other person shall neglect to do so for the space of six hours during the daytime, he shall forfeit and pay the sum of $25 for the first events

[Falco]: 50 for each successive date that the sidewalk shall continue to be encumbered.

[Falco]: B, any person shall not throw or put or cause to be thrown or put any snow or ice into any street in the city.

[Falco]: The fine for violation of this section shall be for the first offense $50, for the second offense and subsequent offenses $100.

[Falco]: The language of said section 74-14 shall hereby be amended to read as follows.

[Falco]: Section 74-114, removal of snow and ice.

[Falco]: A, whenever snow or ice accumulates on a sidewalk, the owner of any land or building abutting a sidewalk or walking path shall remove the snow and ice to permit safe passage for pedestrians on the sidewalk abutting the owner's property and the entrance to the pedestrian crossing abutting the sidewalk.

[Falco]: The owner shall also remove snow at a fire hydrant within or abutting the sidewalk that abuts the owner's property sufficient to

[Falco]: allow fire department access to the hydrant.

[Falco]: The owner shall remove the snow or ice or treat the sidewalk with sand or any other suitable material to permit safe passage to pedestrians.

[Falco]: The owner shall remove snow and ice within six daylight hours after the snow stops falling and the city may extend the deadline set forth above in its discretion.

[Falco]: The city's code enforcement officer or his designee or the police department shall notify the owner of the failure to comply and allow the owner 24 hours to comply.

[Falco]: For residential properties, if the owner does not comply within 24 hours of receiving notice, the city may in its discretion remove.

[Falco]: removal as a lien on the owner's property tax to fine the owner $50 per day until the owner complies.

[Falco]: For such subsequent offense within 12 months, the fine or charge shall double.

[Falco]: For commercial properties, if the owner does not comply within 24 hours of the receiving notice, the city may, in its discretion, remove the snow or ice and charge the owner for the removal as a lien on the owner's property tax bill

[Falco]: will fine the owner $100 per day until the owner complies.

[Falco]: For each subsequent offense within 12 months, the fine or charge shall double.

[Falco]: B, a person shall not throw or put or cause to be thrown or put any snow or ice into any street in the city.

[Falco]: The fine for violation of this section shall be, for residential property owners, $50 for the first offense, $100 for the second offense and subsequent offenses.

[Falco]: The fine for commercial property owners, $100 for the first offense and $200 for the second offense and subsequent offenses.

[Falco]: June 0-356, joint resolution to petition the federal government for emergency financial relief.

[Falco]: It is hereby resolved by her honor, the mayor Breanna Lungo-Koehn, the Honorable Medford City Council and the Honorable Medford School Committee that whereas on March 11th, 2020, the World Health Organization designated the COVID-19 outbreak

[Falco]: pandemic health emergency.

[Falco]: And whereas on March 20th, 2020, the governor of the Commonwealth of Massachusetts issued a declaration of a state of emergency to respond to COVID-19.

[Falco]: And whereas on March 16th, 2020, her honor

[Falco]: The mayor and the Medford Board of Health announced that a local state of emergency exists in the city of Method.

[Falco]: And whereas the public health crisis has precipitated an economic collapse that has affected every sector of the local, state, and national economies.

[Falco]: Whereas, following this collapse, municipalities across Massachusetts and the United States are facing a fiscal crisis that threatens the ability for cities and towns to deliver critical services to our community.

[Falco]: And whereas, the delivery of these services directly and critically affects the quality of life, safety, education, and health of the Medford community, now therefore be it resolved

[Falco]: that the city of Method by her honor, the mayor, the honorable city council and the honorable Medford school committee.

[Falco]: Number one, the federal and state governments by and through the city's elected delegations continue engaging with cities and towns to determine budget needs and solutions at the municipal level.

[Falco]: And number two, the federal and state governments consider it an urgent and emergency need to provide adequate financial support to cities and towns to weather the current economic and fiscal crisis in the form of direct stimulus and relief as soon as possible in order to continue to provide the high quality of critical services upon which the Medford community relies.

[Falco]: The original paper filed in the office of the city clerk

[Falco]: Medford City Hall, Medford, Massachusetts.

[Falco]: 20-090, offered by Council of the Night.

[Falco]: Ordinance establishing an extended illness leave bank.

[Falco]: There shall be an extended illness leave bank for employees of the city who participate therein.

[Falco]: Extended illness advisory board appointment eligibility term.

[Falco]: There shall be an extended illness leave bank advisory board.

[Falco]: This board shall consist of five members that are city employees appointed by the mayor no later than 30 days following passage.

[Falco]: These appointments shall be subject to council approval.

[Falco]: Board members will serve a term of 24 months from the date of council confirmation.

[Falco]: No more than two board members shall be employees at will.

[Falco]: Administration.

[Falco]: The director of personnel shall administer the bank in accord with the rules and regulations established by the Extended Illness Leave Bank Advisory Board and shall be precluded

[Falco]: from serving as a member of this board.

[Falco]: Implementation, participation requirements.

[Falco]: The Extended Illness Advisory Board shall prescribe regulations governing its operation no later than 60 days following confirmation of its fifth member.

[Falco]: The Extended Illness Advisory Board may alter, amend, and update these regulations from time to time thereafter by majority vote of its members.

[Falco]: This shall make one-time investment of 75 leave days to establish the Extended Illness Leave Bank.

[Falco]: Thereafter, any employee of the City who has completed one year of service may participate by donating to said bank any earned sick, personal, or vacation leave time in such amount

[Falco]: with such frequency as said regulation shall permit to maintain a sufficient balance in the bank, but not less frequently than annually.

[Falco]: Upon medical verification pursuant to such regulations, a participating employee with an extended illness who has exhausted all other earned leave

[Falco]: And who has been on leave because of such extended illness for not less than 20 consecutive work days may obtain from said bank additional paid leave or not more than 120 days in any two year period.

[Falco]: Current employees with all other earned leave exhausted who have been on leave because of extended illness shall be eligible to seek benefits from the Extended Illness Leave Bank retroactively to January 1st, 2020.

[Falco]: It shall not be required to donate to said bank any earned sick, personal, or vacation leave time to participate.

[Falco]: Said regulations shall provide safeguards against use of said bank by employees who have improperly used existing sick leave.

[Falco]: The head of each city department shall not less than twice annually provide written notice to each employee of the opportunity to participate in said bank.

[Falco]: Upon receipt of the first such notice, each employee shall be required to sign a form issued by the city indicating that such employee has been informed of the opportunity to participate in said bank.

[Falco]: Nothing contained herein shall affect existing collective bargaining agreements containing provisions relating to the establishment of extended illness leave banks.

[Falco]: Every order and resolution must be endorsed.

[Falco]: Filing of petitions.

[Falco]: For the purposes of the section, the following definitions shall apply.

[Falco]: Order defined as a local bylaw enacted by the City Council.

[Falco]: Resolution defined as a paper stating an expression of opinion, fact, principle, or purpose.

[Falco]: petition defined as an application requesting council action as required by law.

[Falco]: No order or resolution shall be received or acted upon unless endorsed by a member of the council.

[Falco]: The filing of petitions shall be reserved only for matters requiring council action per law, including but not limited to special permits, grants of location, signed variances, and common vigila licenses.

[Falco]: Only petitions filed

[Falco]: Only petitions filed meeting this criteria shall be assigned a council paper number.

[Falco]: The following two definitions are hereby added to section 94-2 entitled definitions.

[Falco]: Brewery means an establishment primarily engaged in the production and distribution of beer, ale, and other malt beverages, which may include accessory uses such as tours of the brewery, retail sales, and or on-site consumption of the products

[Falco]: For example, a tap room or tasting room.

[Falco]: The facility shall hold the appropriate Commonwealth of Massachusetts brewery license, as well as any required pouring license approved by the local licensing authority.

[Falco]: This facility may host marketing events, special events, and brewery tours.

[Falco]: The facility may only sell beverages produced by and commercial goods branded by the brewery.

[Falco]: Tasting room tap room means a room attached to a brewery that allows patrons to sample or consume bear, ale, or other malt beverages that are produced on site in accordance with general law chapter 138.

[Falco]: Barrel means a container, usually cylindrical in nature, used for the storage of a malt beverage with a capacity of not more than 31 gallons.

[Falco]: CC registrar vote is from Adam Hurtubise, City Clerk, regarding Ward 3, Precinct 1 polling location, July 23, 2020.

[Falco]: This is a follow-up paper to 20-472 from last month, as I reported in June.

[Falco]: The former Lawrence Memorial Hospital site will not be available as a polling location for the September-November elections because of the ongoing construction and because of COVID-19 concerns.
